<Review>I love abandoned places and taking cool photos. It's private property so please be careful and respectful if you're looking for some adventure. This place was up and running in the 1960's, and, in it's hayday during the 70's and 80's; the best around for the area; the Marshal Scotty's Amusement Park.
But, now as an abandoned amusement park it's great for a Halloween scare as the haunted park comes alive. Make sure you visit at least once!< /Review>< date>

<user_name>Nicholaus Ewing-Pistelak< /user_name>< Text>
if you're in your mid/late 30s or better you for sure remember marshall scotties... well its not exactly like you rememeber it, but the iconic items like the roller coaster, ferris wheel, bumper cars and the buildings are still all there. However, they've been repurposed in a haunting fashion. The haunted amusement park is a trail that snakes its way through the majority of the park and has plenty of people working the haunted attraction to make sure you keep your guard up. The decorating, lights and theme are well done and its definatley something that you need to experience for yourself or better yet with a friend. Part nostalga and lots of haunted fun.<//Text>

<username>Jessica Waldram< /username><Date>1540700446702< /Date><Rate>5<//Rate>< Text>
This is by far the scariest haunted house I have ever been to! The line to buy the tickets took about 10-15 minutes and then my husband and I spent the $25 each to be able to move straight to the front of the line which was great cause the line is very long. the walk-through takes about 15 to 20 minutes and the entire time there are people jumping out at you chasing you screaming at you and scaring the living life out of you. I literally had to change my pants at the end. It was fun but I wish I would have taken a Valium before hand because it might have made it just a tad bit more enjoyable cause I might have been able to keep my eyes open< /Text>

<review>Did anyone ever get the contact information for the supervising officials of this SF Honduras Consulate Office?  Yesterday we were advised that in order to renew an expired Honduran Passport (expired March 2021) you must present a valid Honduras Identification in addition to a birth certificate and the expired passport.  We had the expired passport and the valid birth certificate, a current green card and valid CA drivers license. <Time>1469747454598< /Time><Rating>1<//Rating><GmapID>0x808e35b876c8b927:0x62c172de25384922</GmapID>< review>
I cannot stress enough how terrible my experience was at this SpeeDee Oil Change location.  For starters, the inside of the waiting area was just as hot and humid as outside. No AC for customers? Spare every expense.
As he drove my manual car into place, I could hear him revving the engine and grinding the clutch. Then about five minutes later, the serviceman comes inside and asks me to come out and look at the engine. He tells me to check out the power steering fluid and how dirty it is, and then compares it to a fresh bottle of fluid. He says "normally we charge $80 for the service, but I'll give you the late afternoon special of $60 since we're already doing your oil."
I tell him no, I only want my oil and filter changed. Very shady behavior.
When they finish changing the oil, the man gets back into my car, starts to back up, then barely rolls forward and immediately drops the clutch from a standstill. My car lurches forward and does unseen damage to my clutch and transmission. I ask the cashier behind the counter "Does that man know how to drive a manual car?"
She ignores me for a few moments while she talks to the servicemen in the shop and after a few laughs with the other gentlemen, she turns and says "oh yeah he can drive."
Clearly not.
After they "finish" my service I present a coupon for $29.99 full service. She then tells me the total is over $42.00. I ask why and she says because my 2004 Mazda 3 requires a special type of oil filter. It has never required a "special" filter.
They pull my car forward and say "thank you, take care." I step inside the car and the floors are even dirtier than when I left the car there. I ask "do you guys clean the floors or no?"
(One of their inspection points is to vacuum the car floor. Says right on the coupon I presented and everywhere else on the website.)
The same man who dropped the clutch in my car says "oh sorry, some of our guys went home early so we're short handed."
There was no one else getting any type of service done, and over four men standing there.
He vacuumed the car and I drove away.

"Professional Oil Change" could not be a more inappropriate way to describe their service.< /review>

<review>Its basically the 'Subway' of pizzas (as in the Subway sandwich place). Definitely innovative (as they're continuously playing with different ideas and themes) from their menu options to their dining atmosphere. The only thing that can be a bit irritating for me is the lack of consistency, mainly with regards to the toppings. I feel that I must point out here that I am vegetarian and probably the pickiest vegetarian ever known to man. I've been hailed as, "the worst vegetarian ever"... I don't deny this about myself, its actually the reason why I immediately fell in love with this place. In the beginning, they had all sorts of non-meat topping options, they introduced me (and more importantly got me addicted) to having corn and broccoli on my pizza. Then BAM! One day, no corn :( and then no broccoli! And then, the same thing the next time and then the next time and then I had finally pieced together that they weren't just, "out" they were discontinued, never to return again :,(
My pizzas looked so sad and plain. And they were. I returned, still hopeful, only to be let down time and again.
When you already have limited options by "choice" and then are also limited by chance (like when they're out of absolutely everything I actually want (and I mean even basil)) it's like, come on guys... (and I don't mean the staff here (they're great) I mean the company in general and/or the person ordering the stuff). Then, I'd forget about how it is (only remembering how it was) when I would happily/mistakenly suggest/agree to go with friends only to be reminded, once again. I eventually started opting for tomatoes (even though I dont like cooked tomatoes; because I can't justify going there for what is essentially a cheese pizza; especially when it costs the same as if I loaded up on every topping). Mainly, it adds some color psychologically "tricking" me to believe that "this isnt just a cheese and pineapple pizza." And while I'm not excited that night, they're not too bad when they're cold the next day :-/ it's something right?
They eventually wooed me back with alternate options I won't mention leaving you to potentially discover them on your own. I only say this because I feel like its really a whole nother corn, broccoli situation (introducing it just to have it disappear never to return). Only in this case I feel they didn't really mean for it to be a "topping" option but was the result of a creative stretch I took as a solution to my topping issue. I've grown to accept the corn deal but it's hit or miss with the staff surrounding said item(s) and I'm fearful it'll just not be an option at any given point. Until then, they're still good. But for most of society, I know none of that matters at all and in fact should probably sound great to you.
They have craft beer on DIY tap, they have(?/used to have) video games you can(?/could) play on their huge TVs with friends, they fixed their old chair problem (that God awful heavy metal dragging across the floor and then continuing to echo for all eternity sound anytime anyone moved them) fixed that, they now have many multiple crust and vegan options (fake meat, daiya, etc) if you're into all that which is a huge plus in my book (even though I don't utilize the options cause I suck) I feel like its progress in the right direction and fully support it and all that jazz. Also, there is free parking and they do have a great drink selection alcoholic and non.<//review>< Pics>
